<p>This article summarizes the events, album releases, and album release dates in <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop music</a> for the year 2011.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January">January</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: January">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shady_Records" title="Shady Records">Shady Records</a> signs <a href="/wiki/Slaughterhouse_(group)" title="Slaughterhouse (group)">Slaughterhouse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yelawolf" title="Yelawolf">Yelawolf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Decon_Records" title="Decon Records" class="mw-redirect">Decon Records</a> signs <a href="/wiki/Roc_Marciano" title="Roc Marciano">Roc Marciano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="February">February</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: February">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>For the rap categories of the 2011 Grammy Awards, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> wins two Grammy Awards for Best Rap Solo Performance and Best Rap Album while <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> wins Best Rap/Sung Collaboration, Best Rap Performance by a Duo or a Group, and Best Rap Song.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> pairs up with auto manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a> to star in a two-minute-long advertisement that aired during the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLV" title="Super Bowl XLV">2011 Super Bowl</a>, which was hailed by critics as being "authentic" and "rousing", and which is reported to have contributed to the boost in Chrysler's first quarter profits.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="March">March</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: March">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Singer <a href="/wiki/Nate_Dogg" title="Nate Dogg">Nate Dogg</a> dies on March 15, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Lasers_(album)" title="Lasers (album)">Lasers</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a> debuts at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, selling 204,000 copies its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-BB-Lasers_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BB-Lasers-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the first rap album to debut at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 in 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April">April</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: April">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Detroit rapper Fuzz Scoota joins the rap group <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Krayzie_Bone" title="Krayzie Bone">Krayzie Bone</a> splits from <a href="/wiki/Bone_Thugs-N-Harmony" title="Bone Thugs-N-Harmony" class="mw-redirect">Bone Thugs-N-Harmony</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>The scheduled May 16 release of Lil Wayne's <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Carter_IV" title="Tha Carter IV">Tha Carter IV</a></i> is delayed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> awarded 100% of the digital royalties from his first album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronic" title="The Chronic">The Chronic</a></i> in a lawsuit from Death Row Records.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lil_B" title="Lil B">Lil B</a> names his new album <i>I'm Gay</i>, sparking controversy and death threats.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="May">May</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: May">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>M-Bone of <a href="/wiki/Cali_Swag_District" title="Cali Swag District">Cali Swag District</a> dies from multiple gun wounds in front of his house in Inglewood, California.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="June">June</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: June">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a> stirs controversy, calling United States President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> "the biggest terrorist in America".<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a> drastically slims down 88 pounds, currently weighing 265 pounds, in reaction to the death of seven of his friends due to obesity.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ja_Rule" title="Ja Rule">Ja Rule</a> begins his two-year prison sentence for gun charges stemming from a 2007 arrest in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The late <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a>'s 40th birthday celebrated on June 16 at a venue in Atlanta, hosted by his mother, <a href="/wiki/Afeni_Shakur" title="Afeni Shakur">Afeni Shakur</a> and comedian <a href="/wiki/Mike_Epps" title="Mike Epps">Mike Epps</a>. Notable performing acts included <a href="/wiki/Erykah_Badu" title="Erykah Badu">Erykah Badu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The manhunt for hip-hop record executive James "Jimmy Henchman" Rosemond ends with his arrest by US Marshals and DEA agents in NY City and a subsequent charge for heading a cocaine trafficking ring.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>It is revealed that <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> is suffering from <a href="/wiki/Graves%27_disease" title="Graves' disease">Graves' disease</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">2Pac's</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Tupac_Shakur_album)" title="Greatest Hits (Tupac Shakur album)">Greatest Hits</a></i> album is certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">diamond</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bad_Meets_Evil" title="Bad Meets Evil">Bad Meets Evil</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Hell:_The_Sequel" title="Hell: The Sequel">Hell: The Sequel</a></i> becomes the first group album to debut at #1 on Billboard 200, but the second hip hop act to have a #1 album in 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shawty_Lo" title="Shawty Lo">Shawty Lo</a> signs a deal with 50 Cent's <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_Records" title="G-Unit Records">G-Unit Records</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="July">July</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: July">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a> is released from prison.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Papers_(Wiz_Khalifa_album)" title="Rolling Papers (Wiz Khalifa album)">Rolling Papers</a></i> is the first rap album to be certified gold in 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Beats,_Rhymes_%26_Life:_The_Travels_of_a_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="Beats, Rhymes &amp; Life: The Travels of a Tribe Called Quest">documentary film</a> is released in the United States, amid a much-publicized disagreement over the film's vision between <a href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(rapper)" title="Q-Tip (rapper)" class="mw-redirect">Q-Tip</a> and director <a href="/wiki/Michael_Rapaport" title="Michael Rapaport">Michael Rapaport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="August">August</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: August">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> publishes Hip Hop Cash Kings 2011, placing <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> first ($37 million), followed by <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Diddy</a> ($35 million). The rest follow as <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> ($16 Million), <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> ($15 Million), <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(rapper)" title="Birdman (rapper)">Birdman</a> ($15 million), <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> ($14 million) <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> ($14 million), <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a> ($11 million) <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> ($6.5 million) and <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a> ($5 million).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Brooklyn rapper Kampane is found dead in a suspected homicide.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Watch_the_Throne" title="Watch the Throne">Watch the Throne</a></i> becomes the fastest-selling rap album in 2011, selling 436,000 copies its first week, beating <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a>'s third studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Lasers" title="Lasers" class="mw-redirect">Lasers</a></i>. It is also the third rap album to debut at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> names <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> "the King of Hip Hop".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> rushed to a hospital in St. Louis from a skateboarding incident, suffering a wound over his eye.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>West and Jay-Z's <i>Watch the Throne</i> becomes the second rap album to earn gold.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>In response to West and Jay-Z's single "<a href="/wiki/H%E2%80%A2A%E2%80%A2M" title="H•A•M">H•A•M</a>", <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> fires back at <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> in his song "It's Good" regarding "Baby's Money". One of the collaborators on the track <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a> denies involvement in the beef. Lil Wayne states there would not be any repercussions. <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)" class="mw-redirect">Drake</a>, the other collaborator, was unaware of the beef at the time of recording.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Rapper <a href="/wiki/Royce_da_5%279%22" title="Royce da 5'9&quot;">Royce da 5'9"</a> releases fifth and final independent album <a href="/wiki/Success_Is_Certain" title="Success Is Certain">Success Is Certain</a> which debuts at #25 on the US Billboard Hot 200.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a> is released from prison.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="September">September</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: September">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Watch_the_Throne" title="Watch the Throne">Watch the Throne</a></i> is certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_JZ-KW_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA_JZ-KW-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pusha_T" title="Pusha T">Pusha T</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a> signs a solo record deal with <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Records" title="Def Jam Records" class="mw-redirect">Def Jam Records</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Carter_IV" title="Tha Carter IV">Tha Carter IV</a></i> sells 965,000 copies its first week, making it the fastest-selling rap album and the overall second-fastest-selling album of the year. It also becomes the fifth rap album to debut at #1 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200. He also has 12 singles appear on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> in the first week of September.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a> was brought back to prison due to conducting business with VH1 reality show producers for his upcoming reality show, delaying his release date to late September. Later, T.I. was released to a halfway house to complete his sentence.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ray_J" title="Ray J">Ray J</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fabolous" title="Fabolous">Fabolous</a> were involved in an altercation with each other in Las Vegas, where the match between <a href="/wiki/Floyd_Mayweather" title="Floyd Mayweather" class="mw-redirect">Floyd Mayweather</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victor_Ortiz" title="Victor Ortiz">Victor Ortiz</a> occurred.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> announced his intent to record two more <i>Tha Carter</i> albums, a joint album with <a href="/wiki/Juelz_Santana" title="Juelz Santana">Juelz Santana</a>, and a second <a href="/wiki/Young_Money" title="Young Money" class="mw-redirect">Young Money</a> compilation album.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October">October</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: October">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>'s debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Cole_World:_The_Sideline_Story" title="Cole World: The Sideline Story">Cole World: The Sideline Story</a></i> sells 218,000 copies in its first week, charting at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV-Cole_Debuts_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-Cole_Debuts-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> has suffered two seizures while traveling to cities to perform.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>It is reported that <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> is recording sequels to <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Not_a_Human_Being" title="I Am Not a Human Being">I Am Not a Human Being</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rebirth_(Lil_Wayne_album)" title="Rebirth (Lil Wayne album)">Rebirth</a></i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> announces that a GOOD Music compilation album will be released sometime in spring 2012.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Rapper/Model <a href="/wiki/Lola_Monroe" title="Lola Monroe" class="mw-redirect">Lola Monroe</a> signs onto <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>'s label Taylor Gang.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November">November</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: November">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Brick Squad Monopoly affiliate RoseMo700 is gunned down in Los Angeles on November 3 while on his way home at the age of 26.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Legendary rapper <a href="/wiki/Heavy_D" title="Heavy D">Heavy D</a> dies at his home in Beverly Hills, California.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pitbull_(rapper)" title="Pitbull (rapper)">Pitbull</a> files a countersuit against <a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Lohan" title="Lindsay Lohan">Lindsay Lohan</a> citing her multiple prison sentences lead to the credibility of the reference and her ineligibility to file her lawsuit in New York, being a California resident.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Erick_Sermon" title="Erick Sermon">Erick Sermon</a> suffers a heart attack.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a> of <a href="/wiki/Three_6_Mafia" title="Three 6 Mafia">Three 6 Mafia</a> signs a solo deal with <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>'s Taylor Gang Records.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Take_Care_(album)" title="Take Care (album)">Take Care</a> solds 630.000 in this debut week, being the second #1 album of <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)" class="mw-redirect">Drake</a>, and the third fastest selling album of 2011 (behind <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="December">December</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_in_hip_hop_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: December">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Strange_Music" title="Strange Music">Strange Music</a> signs <a href="/wiki/Prozak_(rapper)" title="Prozak (rapper)">Prozak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1017_Brick_Squad" title="1017 Brick Squad" class="mw-redirect">1017 Brick Squad</a> affiliate Slim Dunkin is shot and killed in an Atlanta studio.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
